There are a LOT of washing machines all different sizes.  There are also plenty of very large dryers with a sign that says they fit 2 wash loads per dryer.  Washers are pre-set prices (based on load size) and the dryers are $0.25 for 8 minutes.  There are two change machines ($1,$5,$10) and a detergent vending machine with the following choices: Oxi Clean, Bounce, Tide, Gain, Downy, and Clorox2.  There isn't a ton of seating, but this place is pretty clean and there is plenty of parking.  I haven't used too many laundromats, but this one seems good.</review>

< review>
Can't put my finger on it but I find myself coming back here. I first stumbled upon this place 2 years ago when I decided to order wonton noodle soup to-go. I was expecting much, especially since it was take-out but it was actually pretty good. I have a high standards for wontons and dumplings and must admit it's pretty good. Found myself back here again a few weeks ago. I could have went to Hon's, which is my go-to spot for wontons but I wanted to give this place a shot dining in. Wonton noodle soup was what I ordered. Noodles had a great bite to it, better then most places I've been to. Wontons were on point with strong pork and cabbage flavor. Quite different than Hon's but I can see myself preferring this occasionally. Broth was a bit salty but nothing special.< /review>

It's pretty hard to make bad Chinese food, but this place manages to pull it off. I rarely post a bad review but the service here was poor to mediocre and the food was overpriced for what is basically the cheapest and lowest quality Chinese. The brocolli beef was ok (just ok), but the chow Mein was terrible. The meat was seriously questionable: chicken was rubbery and the pork was dry and old. We just ate the noodles and avoided the meat entirely. I gave this place two stars because the food was basically edible, but it was still far from enjoyable.<//review>

<name>Andy Mai<//name>< Text>
Great trail for beginners. There are many benches along the way. The total loop is 5 miles. There is a paved walk way the whole way so you can easily ride a bike or roller blade or even drive a car. The view is great and perfect for family even with kids. There are plenty parking spaces or you can just drive along. Highly recommended !!!</Text>

<user_id>110400146182741479070<//user_id><name>Pranjali Sharma</name>< Time>
1554572613616<//Time>
< rating>
4< /rating>
< text>
Paved trail throughout. Definitely well-trafficked. I got here at 7:30 am on a Saturday and just about managed to find a spot to park. Recommend going clockwise so you can get the shaded areas later. It does get tiring if you plan to jog the whole way, I probably ended walking 1/3 of the route. Keep to the right, get water and sunscreen. Get here early. Chances are, you won't find parking space after 8 am.
Good place to go kayaking or hop onto small boats and fish.<//text>

<gmap_id>0x80dbf941ee6d43f1:0x1892974c8944850c< /gmap_id><name>Autismmama< /name>< Text>
Paved 5 mile round loop around pretty lake. Lots of ducks and other birds. You can rent a Kayak. Fish for Rainbow Trout and Crappie. No waterfowl hunting here, but it's more of a place to hike, ride beach bikes or recreational bikes. Dog friendly, if on leash. Good place for moms to take jogging or average strollers. Lower trails around lake to jog in less crowded setting, but be cautious on weekdays. Not so crowded, and some weird people seen on that lower trail. Usually peaceful on weekdays, but again, bring your dog if you're a female hiking alone, on lower trails.  Avoid weekends if you can't tolerate crowds. And you hate random cars driving on the bike, jogging and walking trail around lake.< /Text>

< text>
Great spot for strollers as we wanted an area to take a leisurely walk and push our daughter around.

Many porta potties that are well maintained around the lake.

There is a snack bar that sells vittles for / after your trip around the lake.

Parking is plentiful. Unless it‚Äôs a major holiday, there isn‚Äôt an issue.

If you want to have a picnic, plenty of tables available near the parking lot or you can drive around the lake (10MPH speed limit) and use one of their picnic areas. I believe they are designated on the map.

Would recommend comfortable walking shoes. There are quite a few cyclists so make sure to follow the path rules of staying to the right, passing on left!<//text>

Want to lose 3 lbs in 1 week?  Then come here at Lake Miramar and walk 5 miles for 5 days.

I don't think I will ever get tired of this place.  Lake Miramar is by far, my all time and number 1 favorite trail.  This is where I think about my whole life, past, present, and future.

First mile = The hardest one.  Why?  Because I still have 4 more miles to go.  It takes me about 1 hour and 45 minutes to walk the whole trail.  Yea, I know....Slow walker.

Second mile = I start to think about going home because I if I turn around now, that would still be 4 miles.  not bad right?

Third mile = Thank goodness, I didn't turn around.  I'm starting to feel motivated and I only have 2 more miles to go.

Fourth mile = I'm starting to feel that I can do this every day.  Maybe I can do sit ups, girly push ups, and knee ups after this.

Fifth mile = Yea...I'm not going to do push up, girly push ups, and knee ups.  I'm just going straight home because my legs are done and I'm starving.

See ya!< /Text>

< text>
This place is wonderful. Depending on your situation they charge either $25 or $50 a night, and in super special situations it's free of charge. A shuttle to and from the hospital is provided every 15 minutes 24/7. But you can't just go in and get a room, UC Davis sets up the reservations. There are 4 shared kitchens, each room has its own mini fridge and cabinet in assigned kitchen to store your own food. They have some items in Each kitchen laid out for people to eat if they aren't able to bring/afford there own room. Each room has it own bathroom though, those aren't shared. Laundry facility provided. no smoking on property, must walk off property to have a cigarette. Free parking for guests. This place is a blessing for families in need that have a loved on at uc Davis.< /text>

< gmapID>
0x809ad0763e6f1295:0x696fb031d1128a0a</gmapID>
</record>
</dataset><record>
<Resp>None< /Resp><text>The Kiwanis Family House (KFH) is similar to the more familiar and nearby Ronald McDonald House. The two big differences are: 1) KFH is for the families of UC Davis patients who live more than 35 miles away from the hospital, not just for the families of children--but any aged patient; and 2) the KFH was founded and continues to be supported by the efforts of regional Kiwanis Club members. The Kiwanis Clubs support the site both monetarily and through service projects. As a more grass-roots option, KFH doesn't have all the bells and whistles of McD's, but they do have what stressed-out families need: a safe place to sleep, eat, and park their vehicles.
Before a guest can stay at KFH, they must be referred by the hospital to KFH. Ask the charge nurse of your floor for help with that. Availability is first-come, first-served, and there are no guarantees. When my aunt and uncle visited, they had to stay in a hotel for 2 nights, but KFH was able to provide them a room for the next 3 nights. The rooms are not free, but they are usually less expensive than nearby hotels. Prices may vary, so check with the charge nurse for the current rates.
Check-in was a bit slow, and they ask a lot more questions than a hotel does, and there are more rules you have to agree to. Nothing terrible, but they want you to treat the place well since it's a community-supported special place. They give you a tour of the facility, pointing out the common areas, your personal refrigerator, the common groceries you can share, the lounges and game room, the places to park, the shuttle stop that takes you to the hospital at no charge, and the free-Internet.
I haven't stayed there myself, but I've helped family and friends settle in there on three different occasions. They all felt the place was a nice haven from the stress, and they appreciated being so close to the hospital. Their only complaint (and they all said the same thing) was that the mattresses made it feel like they were sleeping atop a blimp, where it was rubbery, curvy, and like they would roll off if they weren't careful. My 6'+ uncles both said the beds were also too short for their tall frames to stretch out without their feet falling off the end of the bed. The bathrooms were small, but private and adequate.
There also are RV/camping spaces out back, so if you prefer camping, that is an option, too.
I would give this place a 4.5 star rating if I could, but since I can't, I rounded up to 5 stars. The half-star deduction would mainly be for the beds, the difficulty getting reservations (because there is more need than their limited facilities can provide), and the lengthy check-in process. But all the benefits and the caring nature of the staff are why I rounded up instead of down.<//text><user_name>Will Murray (Willscrlt)</user_name>< gmapID>

<name>chuck leplant<//name>< text>
Food was good. The tables for 2 are small and they expect you to fit the grill, bonchon, plate of meats and the hotpot bowl if you added that. Drinks are party cup size and no refills so it's 1.50 each drink. I wouldn't have minded since I'm glad I can even do kbbq but the service was ridiculously slow. Being seated next to the entrance and having servers pass by every couple of minutes you would think they might stop by and ask if you needed anything. Especially if 15 min have passed and you clearly have no meats left to grill or eat. I spent more time drinking my drink than eating it seemed like. The outdoor model doesn't work like it does indoors where the kitchen is near by and service is fast. I will not be returning until indoor service is available again. The spicy pork belly and the galbi short ribs were my favorite. The premium steak looked like dried dog treats. I didn't get to try any seafood since they forgot it on our second round of meats. I left after that.</text>

< text>
Who doesn't love all-you-can-eat Korean BBQ. this place also gives you the option to add a soup hot pot for an additional $3. But because of weather was warm we opted just for the regular Korean BBQ. We got here about 6:30 and the place was just having people trickle in. By 7 it was pretty packed in here.

So this place you order your dishes by touch screen. You're allowed to order for dishes at a time. So we ordered for and submitted it and some dishes came. Then we ordered some more if you more dishes came. The kitchen was very slow about getting our food out.  and we kept ordering more more food though it didn't seem like much was coming out of the kitchen. Since it was all-you-can-eat we weren't really worried about starving but I had a feeling that not all our food actually came out to our table.  The things we really liked was the marinated short ribs, the red wine marinated pork belly, and and the any of the thinly sliced beef that we ordered. We sat there and ate for almost two hours. We never felt rush and we didn't over eat either.

we got plenty of attention from the serving staff as they were constantly checking up on us and bringing food. Whenever our grill even gotto the point where anything was slightly sticking they would come and change it.

There is a caution sign about parking in the lot and that people should not leave valuables in the car or insight because there have been numerous break-ins.<//text>

<username>Eric Y.< /username><Date>1515988874434</Date>< Rating>

< Text>
Was actually pretty disappointed. Night started off great but just went downhill from there. The Pros: service was good at the get go, they were quick to bring up dishes, they constantly changed our grill in the beginning (maybe even a tad too much). The Bad: Meat quality was not as good as other places (think cartilage, excess fat, or tough cuts), portion sizes were too large (a problem because some of the items just aren't good and you're stuck trying to finish them when all you wanted was to try it), they became completely inattentive after we passed our first hour of eating, their ordering pad was faulty, and they really do stick to their two hour eating limit to a tee and were pretty blunt about it. Most places will use the two hour time limit as a guideline and generally exercise more finesse when it comes time to gently remind you to wrap up. Here they hand you the bill 25 minutes before your time is up and tell you you're almost out of time. No last call for orders, drink refills, or offers to get anything. If two hours sounds adequate, you'll quickly realize it isn't since they seem to count even the time it takes you to sit down, learn how to use their ordering system, and not to mention there's a line for the sauces. We realistically got about 80 minutes of eating time. Add to this the time it takes to grill meats and you'll quickly realize two hours isn't really adequate to actually have a good time. When we got the bill, we were also charged $26.99 for dinner instead of the advertised $25.99 price. +$3 for hot pot person but I thought it was worthwhile since I liked the hot pot more. In terms of selection of meats and veggies, they don't offer as much as other places though we did like that they had oysters which was different and the highlight of our bbq. Recommend coming here for lunch first to see if you like it. Dinner doesn't seem worthwhile to me.<//Text>

<name>Eva L</name>< Text>
Outdoor dining review: Expect a wait for everything. The servers are overwhelmed and understaffed. Management should better support their wait staff with trolleys to help with the load of dishes since the walk is anything but short with their new outdoor set up. Or they should've not bought so many tables for seating as their staff cannot handle the amount of customers that their new set up offers - this was obvious as my group arrived to many available tables but it it took 30 minutes to be seated.

Menu is on paper which is discarded after use so there's no reusing of those. Most beef items are raw and grill-able. Other items are cooked in their kitchen and brought out to you ready to eat. You could also put those on the grill to adjust doneness to your liking - like I like pork belly to be on the golden, crispier side.

Not a great ayce kbbq experience as many of my items were never brought out/had to ask several times for the same thing. My group ended up leaving after 2 hours feeling unsatisfied as we kept waiting and not getting any service. However, I sympathize with the servers as they are ill equipped, overwhelmed, understaffed, and don't have the support they need to keep things running smoothly. Hopefully the management will better provide for their staff. I understand they want to keep up with customer demand (for outdoor dining) but I rather they take care of their staff, the essential workers, that are serving us.< /Text>

<Time>1577863238983</Time><Rating>5</Rating>< review>
This is one of our usual spots for kbbq and as a bonus, they also serve hotpot too. They have a variety of great soups and broth for hotpot but my personal favorite is the mushroom soup. The lunch menu is much smaller than the dinner menu, but it's still good for the price. Pork cheek and chadol are on the lunch menu and really, that's all I need. But they serve, sea food, Korean starter dishes and bonchon. Complimentary sauce bar and you order through a tablet. The staff is pretty quick to help you however you need it. Overall, great place if you like AYCE kbbq and hotpot.</review>

This is not a place you should go solo.  It was my first time as Yelp gave it high ratings.  They seated me in a large booth area (no spots for singles) and I am sure that could be troublesome as my potential is lower than what a group can bring.  I let the server know that it was my first time and she seemed preoccupied as I needed help to explain what to expect.  I am not a fan of cooking my own food and paying for it so I missed that one.  I asked another server who was very helpful to explain some basics and give me his favorite spices to use.  I ordered the popcorn chicken and BBQ beef.  Both were below average on quality of meat.

<Rate>4< /Rate><text>Classic foods with a highly trained team. iPads for ordering directly from the kitchen at every table was welcome. Be prepared to make your own dipping sauce at a communal salad bar like station. It's a fun way to get you even more involved with the food your grilling yourself. The place had an overall clean feel to it, even though my tables iPad was a little busted up. The tables here are also user-friendly and interactive, you can adjust your own temperatures on the Hot Pot grills. On the main Grill I think the server's all have control over it at the end of your table to regulate temperature. The servers do seem, by necessity, to be a little over present in order to make sure you're using all the (more than likely) unfamiliar equipment correctly. It feels a little baby sitterish at times. I had the dessert ice cream. It's a large macaron ice cream sandwich. The macaron taste seems to get in the way of the flavor of whatever ice cream you were getting a bit. I came to Q Pot a while back with my brother as we were both craving Korean bbq and too lazy to drive all the way to Gen! There is a sauce and condiments station that can be a long wait depending how many people is in line.

Their rule is, if 1 person orders both all you can eat grill and all you can eat hot pot, everyone at the table have to too.

<user>110951732799655726110</user>< text>
TL;DR - Henry M. is a phenomenal server. Beef bulgogi and marinated short ribs are 5/5.

Came in, seated promptly in a nice roomy booth. Was quickly greeted by Henry M. in a cool, collected manner, characteristic of a professional proud of his work. Easily someone who's been doing this for awhile, Henry hit every step of service with precision, sometimes in a manner where he got in and out of the table with our refills and requests  without any of us noticing. He even loaded up the first round on the hot plate for us. Best service I've ever received at this restaurant.

As for the food, it was grade A as usual. We ordered the marinated pork belly, spicy beef bulgogi, beef bulgogi, brisket, and premium steak. Ate these dishes with my own sauce made of 3 parts brisket, 1 part ponzu, 1/2 spicy chili sauce, garlic and green onions.

Marinated pork belly: Maybe a bit overcooked on our part, but wasn't brimming with flavor like other dishes. 3/5

Spicy beef bulgogi: Plenty of flavor and juiciness with this one, but definitely on the spicier side. 4/5

Beef bulgogi: great texture to soak up the personal sauce, marinated very well with tons of flavor. 5/5

Brisket: super thin, cooks in seconds. Got the job done. 3/5

Premium steak: juicy, good level of tenderness. Solid fat/meat ratio for a good amount of flavor without
being too fatty. 4/5<//text>

< Review>
The hot pot and KBBQ concept seems cool, but doing both at the same time is overwhelming! You get distracted by all the different items that you don't really get the most of either option. While they offer a variety of meats and seafood, but the quality is mediocre to poor. The best item is the beef tongue so I'll give them that. The hot pot items are okay and they offered some unique items like spam, chinese sausage, and meat filled fish balls. The tom yum soup is really tasty and the taiwanese spicy was pretty good.

If you do plan on visiting, I recommend coming with no more than a party of 4. And do not come HANGRY!! All tables have ONE grill - even the tables that seat 8 people. Do you know how long it takes to cook enough meat to feed that many people?? We had a party of 7 and we probably spent more time waiting for the food to cook than eating it. Plus the ordering system is on one end of the table, so those sitting on the opposite end don't get to see the menu at all.  It is pretty to use, but you have wait 3 minutes before submitting a second order if you get premium items. This is fine, since you can't cook all the meat fast enough on one grill anyway.

Overall, this place is worth a try but not a place I'd frequent.< /Review>

<user_id>100468698028213155517<//user_id><user_name>Ben Falter< /user_name><time>1469978682772</time>< Rating>
2</Rating>
< review>
Mixed Feelings about this restaurant.  Lets break it down.  The restaurant I've been told is only in its second month of operation but is STILL working out some kinks in service and its menu.

The concept is to combine a traditional Korean BBQ & Hot-Pot restaurants into one AYCE experience at your table together.  The service is a mix of traditional servers, people who seem to be running food, and self-ordering from a built-in tablet at the table.  The tablet seems to work pretty well, menus easy to navigate, and good visuals built in (part of the HINTS system).  The self-pay system isn't activated yet and they only accept 2 credit cards per table (so get ready to Venmo friends).  The food selection seems to be pretty good in variety for both hot pot & bbq; and some items we found you could use in both styles.  A self-serve dipping sauce bar was pretty awesome.  The restaurant visually was in great condition, sleek, modern, and with plenty of exhaust hoods.  The meats & veggies were pretty good; not the best I've had but not poor quality.

What I didn't enjoy:  No prices listed on website, in the restaurant, but word of mouth told us it was $25 for both AYCE; not until we waited, then sat did the server offer up that the price has now increased $28 (I believe) which isn't horrible but would be nice if you posted this and were transparent. With plenty of exhaust hoods it certainly didn't seem like ours was working at all; steam and smoke was definitely not going up ours but seemed to trail the next tables vent.  I've heard friends say it was too cold from theirs working.  So this doesn't seem consistent yet.  Ventilation in this style restaurant is highly important.    The service; while our server, Huy, was cheerful and happy guy, he didn't seem to be fast with getting items out to us or knowing where we were in terms of getting the items we ordered.  Pressing the 'help' button on the table didn't seem to equate to him coming over, more my eyes tracking him down worked better.  ICE in the summer; I've seen this as an issue on other reviews and we experienced it too; sorry no ice right now... and then none came later either.  If you split a check (which is most customers) be aware that the suggested tipping amount on the bottom of your customized bill is still the amounts for the full bill but not noted.  Adam the manager I spoke to about this acknowledge this after I called in; I don't think that is a wise and transparent practice.   Some items ordered in the system never came, some only came when we placed a second order into the system.  But by far the most frustrating is that it took 18 minutes for us to receive the lukewarm soup base which took 10 minutes to get to a boil; so 28 minutes in we could start eating.

Be aware its new and popular so you should expect a wait; we waited 1hr 10min; they estimated an hour so no points off for this; just helping you know the reality.  Should you wait?  If you want to try it out; hope they've worked through some things by then.  The food was okay, service needs improvement, their process needs a lot of improvement, and my conversation with the manager didn't seem to address much at all.  Good Luck!<//review>
